<p>The <b>1972 United States House of Representatives elections</b> was an election for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a> in 1972 which coincided with the landslide <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1972" title="United States presidential election, 1972">reelection victory</a> of President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>. Nixon's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party">Republican Party</a> managed to gain a net of twelve seats from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic_Party" title="United States Democratic Party">Democratic Party</a>, although the Democrats retained a majority. This was the first election that citizens at least 18 years of age (instead of 21 and older) could vote due to the recent passage of the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-sixth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-sixth Amendment to the United States Constitution">26th Amendment</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="November_elections">November elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1972&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: November elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alabama"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Alabama" title="List of United States Representatives from Alabama">Alabama</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1972&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alabama was reapportioned from 8 to 7 seats and eliminated the old 3rd district, dividing it between the old 2nd and 4th and making compensating boundary changes elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martis_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-martis-4">[4]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alaska"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Alaska" title="List of United States Representatives from Alaska">Alaska</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1972&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Alaska">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Incumbent Nick Begich won re-election three weeks after having disappeared in a plane crash October 16; challenger Don Young would later win a March special election after Begich was declared dead on December 29.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arizona"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Arizona" title="List of United States Representatives from Arizona">Arizona</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1972&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Arizona">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="California"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_California" title="List of United States Representatives from California">California</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1972&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: California">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>California was reapportioned from 38 to 43 seats, adding one seat in the Bay Area, one in the Central Valley, and 3 in southern California;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martis_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-martis-4">[4]</a></sup> three went to Democrats, two to Republicans. Despite a retirement and two lost renominations, both parties held their seats in this election, bringing the Democrats up from 20 seats to 23 and the Republicans up from 18 seats to 20.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colorado"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Colorado" title="List of United States Representatives from Colorado">Colorado</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1972&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Colorado">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Colorado was reapportioned from 4 to 5 seats, constructing a new 5th district east and south of Denver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martis_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-martis-4">[4]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iowa"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Iowa" title="List of United States Representatives from Iowa">Iowa</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1972&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Iowa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Iowa was reapportioned from 7 seats to 6, dividing the old 5th district around Des Moines between its neighbors. Its incumbent, Neal Smith, won again in the south-central Iowa 4th district.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martis_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-martis-4">[4]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana"><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Representatives_from_Louisiana" title="List of United States Representatives from Louisiana">Louisiana</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections,_1972&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Louisiana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Louisiana stayed at eight house seats following the 1970 census, but the Eighth District's boundaries were radically altered. New governor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edwin_W._Edwards" title="Edwin W. Edwards">Edwin W. Edwards</a>ordered the district to take in territory far to the south and east of its traditional base of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Louisiana" title="Alexandria, Louisiana">Alexandria</a>, which included many African-American and progressive white voters. The change was largely regarded as an election deal between Edwards and former Rep. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gillis_Long" title="Gillis Long">Gillis Long</a>, who finished third in the Democratic Primary in the 1971 Louisiana Governor's Election. Long easily won back the Eighth District seat he lost in 1964.</p>
